Project Implementation Plan                   - 103 -                                      ANNEX A
Vm. COMPONENT DESCRIPTION
FOR POLICY ANALYSIS UNIT
187.  Parliament's adoption of the Government's "Agricultural Policy Strategy" has paved the way for
widespread policy reform over the next 2-3 years. The MAF's capacity for policy analysis and policy
formation is rather limited however, consisting of a unit of two people which reports to the Deputy
Minister, Agriculture Policy. Neither of these people are well-trained in the techniques of policy
analysis.
188.  Recognizing this deficiency, the MAF has now received permission to increase this unit to 4-5
people and has the project support which would establish an effective Agriculture Policy Analysis Unit.
The proposed role, structure and organization of this Agriculture Policy Analysis Unit (APAU) are
outlined below, together with a description of the technical assistance requested from the Project. This
technical assistance has been designed to meet both the immediate needs of MAF to develop the policies
needed to implement the Agricultural Policy Strategy, and the more fundamental long-term need to
establish a strong national policy capacity for policy analysis.
A. ROLE FOR THE MAF POLICY UNIT
189.  Price and trade policy is viewed as the most appropriate focus of the Policy Unit. As the Croatian
economy becomes more open and market-oriented, a strong capacity for price and trade policy analysis
would become increasingly important in order to provide effective advice on:
-  the implications of policy change for Croatian farmers, processors and  consumers of
agricultural products.
- the form which current and future price and trade policies should take
190.  To fulfill this general mandate, MAF would establish a APAU which reports to the Deputy
Minister responsible for economic policy. Working together with the Minister and Deputy-Ministers of
Agriculture, and national and international experts, the specific responsibilities of the APAU would be
to:
- Provide advice on the price and trade policy measures required to implement the agricultural
strategy, and the timing of any policy changes.
- Assist in the preparation, negotiation and re-negotiation of trade agreements which effect the
agricultural sector.
- Monitor trends in domestic and international markets for those agricultural inputs and outputs
relevant to Croatian agriculture, and advise the MAF on the implications of these trends for
agricultural production and trade.
- Monitor trends in domestic agricultural production and agro-processing and advise the MAF
on the implications of these trends for agricultural production and trade.
-  Monitor trends in those macroeconomic conditions which influence production, processing,
prices and trade (inflation, exchange rates, interest rates, economic growth etc)
- Monitor proposed policy changes in other sectors of the economy and advise the MAF on the
implications of these policies for agricultural production and trade.



ANNEX A                                        - 104 -                       Project Implementation Plan
-  Maintain effective links with the agricultural research community and the Agricultural
Research Council.
B. STRUCTURE OF THE POLICY UNIT
191.  The unit would comprise 4-5 people working under a unit head, who would report to the Deputy
Minister responsible for economic policy. In addition to the head person, the unit would require three-
four specialists to work in the following subject areas:
- International Trade and Prices
- Farm Management and Farm Surveys
-  Domestic Marketing, Consumption and Agro-Processing
-  Information Acquisition, Management and Dissemination; and Administrative Support.
192.  In addition to their specific responsibilities, all the staff of the Policy Unit would need to be
computer literate, particularly with word-processing and the use of spread-sheets, and have the ability and
the desire to learn new approaches to economic analysis quickly.
C. JOB DESCRIPTIONS AND QUALIFICATIONS OF POLICY UNIT STAFF
Policy Unit Head
193.  The Policy Unit Head would have overall responsibility for using resources within the unit to
review the implications of current and future policies relevant to the agricultural sector, and advising the
Minister and Deputy-Minister on the form and timing of any policy changes under review. To fulfill this
role he or she would have the following responsibilities:
194.  Responsibilities:
-   Collaborate with the Minister and Deputy Minister in selecting the policy issues to be
examined and monitored by the Policy Unit
-  Allocate these studies and responsibilities to appropriate staff within the Policy Unit and
advise on the most appropriate methodologies and sources of data to use, and the time-frame
in which the work should be completed.
-  Where necessary, take responsibility for the final analysis and report (in the event that the
level of analysis required exceeds the skills of the staff allocated to the study).
- Contract required studies to domestic and international agencies as necessary.
-  Monitor trends and events within and outside the agricultural sector (both in and outside
Croatia) and report to the Minister and Deputy-Minister on their implications for agricultural
policy.
195.  Qualifications:
-  Post-graduate qualification in economics, agricultural economics or a related discipline; an
understanding of market-oriented economic policies and modern approaches to price and trade
policy analysis; experience in staff management.



Project Implementation Plan                      - 105 -                                        ANNEX A
-  A comprehensive understanding of the problems faced by the agricultural sector and the
nature and implications of the policies implicit in Croatia's agricultural strategy.
-  The willingness and ability to leam and apply new approaches to policy analysis.
International Trade and Price Specialist:
196.  Responsibilities:
- Monitor trends in prices, quantities and trading patterns in world markets for relevant
agricultural inputs and outputs, and advise the Unit Head on the implications of these trends.
-  Provide information as required on future world prices, based on projections published by
the World Bank, FAO, OECD and the EU.
-  Where required, use conventional partial equilibrium analysis techniques to determine the
economic and welfare implications of different forms and levels of price support.
-  Monitor trends in agricultural imports and exports and advise the Unit Head on the
implications of these trends.
-  Understand all current and pending bilateral and multilateral trade agreements which affect
the agricultural sector, and advise the Unit Head on factors relevant to the negotiation or re-
negotiation of these agreements
197.  Qualifications:
-  Graduate or post-graduate qualification in economics or agricultural economics, with
particular emphasis on price and trade policy.
-  A knowledge of partial-equilibrium analysis, and world trade in agricultural inputs and
outputs.
-  A knowledge of Croatia's current price policy, agricultural trade and the implications of
future membership of the WTO and the EU.
-  The willingness and ability to learn and apply new approaches to policy analysis.
Farm Management and Farm Survey Specialist:
198.  Responsibilities:
-  Monitor trends in farm output and input prices and their impact on farm production and
profitability, and advise the Unit Head on the implications of these trends.
-  Monitor trends in farm production and the allocation of land to different enterprises, and
advise the Unit Head on the implications of these trends.
-  In conjunction with other relevant groups, plan and coordinate farm surveys and collate the
information collected in order to provide a comprehensive data base on farm households and
enterprises.
-  Based on this survey data and other relevant information, prepare and regularly update
enterprise and full-farm budgets for all types of farmers in selected locations, as the basis for
reviewing on-farm opportunities and constraints.
-  Meet regularly with farmers and extension agents in order to keep informed of the
opportunities and constraints faced by farmers, and the impact of policy change; and advise
the Unit Head on types of information and analyses which would improve the ability of the
Policy Unit to examine these issues.



ANNEX A                                        -106 -                         Project Implementation Plan
199.  Qualifications:
-  Graduate or post-graduate qualification in agricultural economics or agricultural science, with
particular emphasis on farm management.
-  A knowledge of full and partial-budgeting techniques, and trends in domestic production and
prices; and farm survey design, implementation and analysis.
-  A knowledge of the problems faced by Croatia's farmers and the implications of the Croatian
agricultural strategy for their future.
-  The willingness and ability to learn and apply new approaches to policy analysis.
Domestic Marketing, Consumption and Agro-Processing Specialist:
200.  Responsibilities:
-  Monitor trends in domestic supply and demand for agricultural products and advise the Unit
Head on the implications of these trends.
-  Monitor trends in the level and efficiency of agro-processing, and the extent to which this is
influenced by price and trade policy and advise the Unit Head on the implications of these
trends.
-  Provide technical advice on the operation and application of the proposed Market Information
System.
-  Apply conventional partial-equilibrium techniques to analyze the impact of changes in price
and trade policy.
-  Meet regularly with producers associations, consumer groups and agro-processors to keep
informed of the opportunities and constraints which they face, and the impact of policy
change on marketing, processing and consumption; and advise the Unit Head on types of
information and analyses which would improve the ability of the Policy Unit to examine these
issues.
201.  Qualifications:
-  Graduate or post-graduate qualification in agricultural economics, economics, business
administration or food technology, with particular emphasis on marketing and price policy.
-  A knowledge of partial-equilibrium analysis, and the nature of domestic production and
consumption of agricultural inputs and outputs.
-  A knowledge of current issues relevant to domestic agricultural markets and processing, and
the implications of the agricultural strategy for these issues.
- The willingness and ability to learn and apply new approaches to policy analysis.
Information Acquisition, Management. Dissemination: and Administrative Support Specialist
202.  Responsibilities:
-  Establish an information center which provides the MAF with access to relevant data on
domestic and world prices; domestic and international production and trade; farm-level data
and market information.
-  Manage and coordinate the acquisition, use and dissemination of this information
-  Manage and coordinate the proposed Marketing Information System.
-  Provide administrative and technical support to the unit as required



Project Implementation Plan                    - 107 -                                     ANNEX A
These responsibilities could also be assumed by other staff within the Policy Unit.
203.  Qualifications:
-  Graduate qualification in agricultural economics or other related discipline.
-  Familiarity with the sources of data produced by relevant public and private sector
organizations.
- The willingness and ability to learn and apply new skills, should this prove necessary.
D. STAFF TRAINING
204.  Each of the 4-5 staff members would receive up to three months training outside Croatia, in their
field of specialization. In order to complete this training as early as possible, relevant training programs
would be identified as soon as the Project starts. The objective would be to train two specialists in the
first year of the Project and the remaining two-three staff members during the following eighteen months.
Potential training programs include those offered by the Economic Development Institute, World Bank
(USA); the Harvard Institute of International Development, Harvard University (USA); and Wye College,
England. In the course of normal work for the Policy Unit additional experience should also be sought
from attendance at policy seminars and visits to international organizations, within and outside Croatia.
205.  Staff would also receive on-the-job training from the Technical Assistance expert assigned to the
Project. This would include guidance on the choice and application of analytical techniques, supported
where necessary by the acquisition of suitable text-books (with project funds).
E. PHASED ESTABLISHMENT OF THE POLICY UNIT
206.  Initial priority should be given to recruitment of the specialists in International Trade and Prices,
and Marketing and Consumption. These specialists would provide the support needed to address the
immediate needs for trade and price policy issues and the probable investment in market infrastructure.
207.  To ensure that all aspects of agricultural policy are addressed by the APAU, any initial work on
farm management analysis and farm surveys would be contracted out to the Institute of Agriculture.
TECHNICAL ASSISTANCE
(i)    LONG-TERM POLICY ADVISER
208.  To support the establishment and initial operation of the Policy Unit a consultant would be
employed by the Project for a minimum of 18 months, extendable to 24 months at the discretion of the
project. The consultant would work as a Policy Adviser at the level of Specialist and report to the Deputy
Minister responsible for Economic Policy.
209.  While the consultant would be expected to provide immediate technical input into all relevant
areas of policy analysis, his or her overall responsibility would be to develop the capacity of Croatian
staff to fulfill the role and functions of the Policy Unit.



ANNEX A                                          - 108 -                        Project Implementation Plan
210.  Responsibilities:
- Provide guidance to the Deputy Minister and Policy Unit staff on the analysis and choice of
policy measures required to implement the Agricultural Strategy, including all aspects of
price, trade, marketing, farm management and credit policy; and the analysis of issues
relevant to negotiation of trade agreements which affect the agricultural sector.
- Assist staff training through the choice of external training programs, and on-going training
in the choice and application of analytical techniques (supported where necessary by the
acquisition and use of appropriate reference materials).
- Guide the establishment and initial operation of the Market Information System; and assist
with the design, implementation and analysis of the farm management baseline and
monitoring surveys.
- Provide guidance on the type of information which the Policy Unit should have or have
access to, and develop procedures for obtaining, managing and using this information.
- Provide guidance on techniques for monitoring trends in key indicators of agricultural
production, processing, prices and trade.
- Provide guidance on techniques for monitoring trends in key indicators of macro-economic
conditions.
- The consultant should not be directly involved in project management or implementation.
211.  Qualifications:
- Post-graduate qualification in Agricultural Economics or Economics (minimum Master's
Level) with at least five years of experience in agricultural sector policy and a specialization
in either price, trade or marketing issues.
- An understanding of the problems faced by economies in transition, preferably in eastern and
central Europe.
-  A sound grasp of the principles and techniques of economic analysis and the ability to apply
these skills to current problems and issues; and the ability to impart this knowledge to Policy
Unit Staff. The ability to speak and/or read Croatian would also be an advantage.
(ii)   SHORT-TERM PRICE and TRADE SPECIALIST
212.  As it will take some time to staff the Policy Unit, more immediate short-term technical assistance
is needed to begin the policy reforms specified in the Agricultural Strategy. Among the most pressing
reforms are trade and price policy measures related to pending membership of the World Trade
Organization, and the rationalization of import protection and price support. Rapid, well-conceived
policy initiatives in these areas would also help to sustain widespread initial support for the Agricultural
Strategy.



Project Implementation Plan                    - 109 -                                     ANNEX A
213.  To support the analysis, choice and design of these reforms, and the concurrent negotiation and
re-negotiation of major trade agreements, a consultant would be employed as soon as possible for a period
of three months. The consultant would work in the current Policy Department in the MAF and report to
the Deputy Minister responsible for Economic Policy. The MAF would provide the consultant with an
office, computer facilities, and full logistical support. To expedite provision of this technical assistance
it would be funded from the Japanese Grant.
214.  Responsibilities:
- To advise the Deputy Minister on all aspects of price and trade policy, with particular
emphasis on the impact of membership of the World Trade Organization, the rationalization
of import protection and price support, and the negotiation and re-negotiation of major trade
agreements.
- To prepare short written reports on all analyses undertaken in this regard for future reference
by Policy Unit Staff. These reports should describe the issue analyzed, the techniques
applied, and any assumptions used; followed by discussion of the recommendations made.
215.  Qualifications:
- Post-graduate qualification in Agricultural Economics or Economics (minimum Master's
Level) with at least five years of experience in the analysis of price and trade policy.
- A sound knowledge of: the World Trade Organization and the technical aspects of the
Uruguay Round Agreement; the trade implications of the Common Agricultural Policy of the
European Union; and an understanding of the process of negotiating trade agreements.
- An understanding of the problems faced by economies in transition, preferably in eastern and
central Europe.
-  A sound grasp of the principles and techniques of economic analysis and the ability to apply
these skills to the analysis of price and trade policy.
216.  The following gives the consultant requirements (including detailed description of the assignment,
qualification required, and expected output) for the three activities under this assignment: (i) short term
price and trade specialist; (ii) market information system development; and (iii) farm surveys.
F. AGRICULTURE PRICE AND TRADE SPECLILIST
217.  Background. As the Croatian economy becomes more open and market-oriented, price and trade
policy will become increasingly important. A strong capacity for price and trade analysis is thus essential
in order to provide effective advice on:
- the implications of policy change for Croatian farmers and processors and Croatian consumers
of agricultural products; and
- the form which current and future price and trade policies should take.

218.  To fulfill this general mandate the MAF proposes to establish an Agriculture Policy Unit which
reports to the Deputy Minister of Agriculture responsible for economic policy. Working together with
the Minister and Deputy-Ministers of Agriculture, and national and experts, the specific responsibilities
of this Policy Unit would be to:
- Provide advice on the price and trade policy measures required to implement MAF's
Agricultural Policy Strategy, and the timing of any policy changes.
- Assist in the preparation, negotiation and re-negotiation of trade agreement effect the
agricultural sector.
- Monitor trends in domestic and international markets for those agriculture inputs and outputs
relevant to Croatian agriculture, and advise the MAF on the implication of these trends for
agricultural production and trade.
- Monitor trends in domestic agricultural production and agro-processing and advice the MAF
on the implications of these trends for agricultural production.
- Monitor trends in macroeconomic conditions which influence production, processing, prices
and trade (inflation, exchange rates, interest rates, economic growth);
- Monitor proposed policy changes in other sectors of the economy and advise MAF on the
implications of these policies for agricultural production and trade.
219.    Assignent. As it will take some time to staff and equip the Policy Unit, more immediate
technical assistance is needed to begin the policy reforms specified in MAF's Agriculture Policy Strategy.
Among the most pressing of these reforms are those associated with trade and price policy as a result of
pending membership of the World Trade Organization and the proposed rationalization of import
protection and price support. Rapid, well-conceived policy initiatives in these areas will also do much to
sustain the widespread initial support for the Agriculture Policy Strategy and to assist in the restructuring
of MAF's Agriculture Policy Unit.
220.  To support the analysis, choice and design of these reforms, and the concurrent negotiation and

Policy Department in the MAF and report to the Deputy Minister responsible for Economic Policy. The
MAF will provide the consultant with an office, computer facilities, and full logistical support.
221.  Responsibilities and Output. (i) To advise the Deputy Minister on all aspects of price and trade
policy, with emphasis on the impact of membership to the World Trade Organization, rationalization of
import protection and price support, and the negotiation of major trade agreements. (ii) To prepare short
written reports on all analyses undertaken in this regard for future reference by Policy Unit Staff. These
reports should describe the issue analyzed, the methodology applied, and any assumptions used; followed
by discussion of the recommendation
222.  Qualifications: Post-graduate qualification in Agricultural Economics or Economics (minimum

sound knowledge of the World Trade Organization and the technical aspects of the Uruguay Round
Agreement; the trade implications of the Common Agricultural Policy of the European Union; and an
understanding of the process of negotiating trade agreements. An understanding of the problems faced
by economies in transition, preferably in eastern and central Europe. A sound grasp of the principles and
techniques of economic analysis and the ability to apply these skills to the analysis of price and trade
policy and to communicate the associated methodology and results.

G. MARKET INFORMATION SYSTEM
223.  Background. Full access to information is an essential pre-requisite for an efficient, agricultural
sector, especially if family farms are to benefit from the opportunities created by well-functioning
markets. With this in mind, a market information system (MIS) is to be established within MAF's APAU.
The objective is to collect information at approximately ten produce markets throughout Croatia on a
daily basis which would be transmitted to Zagreb by computer for collation and then disseminated through
daily radio broadcasts.
224.  A series of short-term technical inputs would be required to establish the MIS and to review its
initial performance. These inputs would be provided by a Market Information Specialist and a
Communications Specialist who would be employed for 7 weeks and 2 weeks respectively over a total
elapsed time of approximately 5 months. Their respective activities and responsibilities are specified
below.
225.   The technical assistance would involve an initial visit by the market information specialist and
the communication specialists to design the system, arrange the radio broadcasts, and define the technical
specifications of the equipment. Once the hardware and software have been obtained during early project
implementation, the communications specialist would return to install it and check that it was operating
correctly. The market information specialist would then train the enumerators responsible for data
collection and MAF's market policy analyst responsible for data collation, and ensure that they were able
to operate the equipment. Three months after the system has been in operation the market information
specialist would return for a further two weeks to review the system and assess the need and nature of
any improvements.
226.  Detailed Assignments for the Market Information Specialist and the Communications Specialist
A. System Design
- Choose market sites and commodities (types and quality)
-  Determine which information to collect (prices, quantities, quality, origin of produce etc)
- Design and produce questionnaires or survey instruments
- Determine technical specifications of hard and software in collaboration with MAF's
Information officer
- Develop methodology for data collection
-  Establish a format for collating and summarizing the data at the Policy Unit
- Initiate recruitment of enumerators (desired qualifications, amount of work required etc)
- Determine optimal broadcasting procedures
Time Required: 1 month for the Market Information Specialist, two weeks for the
Communications Specialist.
Output:       The output of the design stage would consist in a systematic operational
handbook, discussed and agreed upon with MAF covering all procedural aspects
of the market information system, and including technical specifications of the
hard and software to be procured under the project.



ANNEX A                                        - 112 -                       Project Implementation Plan
B. Training of Enumerators and of MAF's Market Analyst
-     Train enumerators in data collection, data entry and data transmission
-     Train market analyst in data collation, analysis and dissemination of information to radio
stations.
Time Required: 2 weeks for the Market Information Specialist
Output:       Training Curricula and Course
C. Review system after three months of operation
-     Review response to mnarket information provided and perceptions of its usefulness.
-     Recommend changes to the type of information collected, and the manner of collection
and dissemination as considered appropriate.
Time Required: 1 week for the Market Information Specialist
Output:       Evaluation Report
227.  Qualifications:
Market Information Specialist: Degree in (agriculture) marketing (minimnum Master level) or
related fields and at least ten years relevant experience in market intelligence.
Communications Specialist: technical expert in data transfer and processing technology with at
least ten years relevant experience.
H. FARM MONITORING SURVEYS
228.  Background. Prior to independence the collection of agricultural statistics was oriented towards
production on ex-social sector farms. The consequent lack of information on private farms has become
a serious constraint to policy analysis, especially following the adoption of a new Agricultural Policy
Strategy which emphasizes the role of family farms. It is difficult to respond effectively to the needs of
Croatia's small-scale family farms when so little is known about the constraints they face and implications
of policy change for their well-being. To address this problem the project would initiate and fund two
related surveys, each of which covers both full and part-time small-scale family farms. The first would
be a comprehensive baseline survey to provide up-to-date information on factors such demographic
characteristics, the farm resource base, cropping patterns and livestock holdings, levels of production and
marketed surplus, the level and composition of farm income and expenditure, and the contribution of
non-farm income to total household income. It would also include behavioral and attitudinal variables.
A smaller, second survey would then be initiated as the basis for an annual monitoring of the status of
and the changes on family farms. This second survey would be of a size (in terms of both numbers and
data collected) which allows rapid data collection, processing and analysis. The two surveys would be
designed together to ensure that they complement each other as much as possible.
229.  Technical assistance for these surveys would consist of an agriculture statistician and a farm
management survey specialist. Particular emphasis would be placed on involving members of the MAF,



Project Implementation Plan                      - 113 -                                       ANNEX A
the Institute of Agriculture Economics and family farmer representatives in the initial design of the two
surveys. To ensure that the information generated informs policy decisions in a timely manner, careful
attention should also be given to procedures which allow quick and effective data processing. Such
timeliness will be especially important for the smaller annual monitoring surveys.
230.  The duties and responsibilities of the respective consultants are outlined below. An input of two
weeks is envisaged for the agricultural statistician and six weeks for the farm management survey
specialist. The MAF would provide office space and logistical support to each consultant.
231.  Output of the overall assignment: The output of the study would consist in a systematic
operational handbook, discussed and agreed upon with MAF covering all procedural aspects of the
baseline and the on-farm monitoring system.
232.  Agriculture Statistician
Responsibilities:
- together with the Croatian Bureau of Statistics, review the national sampling framework and
develop recommendations on optimal sampling procedures and sample sizes for both the baseline
survey and the annual monitoring surveys.
- review the current definitions of full and part-time farmers used in the national sampling
framework. Decide on their relevance to the two surveys and recommend alternative definitions
where appropriate, plus measures to modify the sampling framework accordingly.
- for the monitoring survey review the implications of taking a new sample each year or
retaining a fixed sample and re-weighing it each year to reflect changes in the underlying
population. Describe the sampling techniques to be used in the event that a new sample is taken
each year, and the basis for re-weighing the sample in the event that a fixed sample is considered
optimal.
- prepare a report of not more than twenty pages which describes the national sampling
framework, its suitability as the basis for the proposed farm surveys, the definitions of full a part-
time farmers, and the sampling procedures and sample sizes considered optimal for each of the
two surveys. Include the description and discussion of the alternative sampling strategies for the
monitoring surveys.
Time allowed for the study and report writing, two weeks.
Qualifications: Advanced degree in agricultural statistics or statistics (minimum Masters Level),
with at least ten years experience in the statistical design of both large and small-scale surveys
of small farmers.



ANNEX A                                           - 114 -                         Project Implementation Plan
233.  Farm Management Survev Specialist
Responsibilities:
- together with staff of the MAD, Institute of Agriculture Economies and small-farner
representatives, determine the principle issues which information from the Baseline and
Monitoring surveys should seek to illuminate.
- based on these issues, develop and test the questionnaires for both surveys, to collect both
quantitative and qualitative infornation (attitudes, perceptions of constraints and opportunities
etc). Ensure that the two sets of questionnaires generate data which are consistent and can be
used in a complementary manner.
- for the monitoring survey questionnaire, ensure that one element of the data set is quantitative
and constant, to provide a consistent source of time-series data; and another more flexible module
collects on issues of current importance. (for example the use of a permanent module on factors
such as resource use, cropping patterns and livestock holdings, production levels and marketed
surplus; plus a qualitative module which varies from year to year in response to particular issues
of importance).
- determine the most appropriate definitions of full and part-time farmers based on the report by
the agricultural statistician and discussions with Croatian collaborators.
- based on the sampling strategies recommended by the agricultural statistician, develop a cost-
effective strategy for sample selection for each survey, which facilitates accurate, efficient
collection. include consideration of interviews, mail surveys, and the payment of farmers to keep
their won records and complete their own questionnaires.
- develop data entry and verification routines in association with questionnaire design, to sure that
the data are entered and checked in a timely manner; and make realistic estimates of the time and
resources required to transform the raw data into a form useful for analysis.
- advise on the most appropriate basis for analysis of the data from each survey, and prepare an
outline report (including dummy tables), to guide final analysis and ensure that the results
illuminate the issues originally defined.
- for each survey prepare a realistic timetable for survey implantation and data processing and
analysis.
- prepare a report which summarizes the issues to be addressed by the two surveys, the sampling
strategies and data collection and processing techniques to be used, the implementation timetables,
and the outline of the analysis. Time required to complete the study, including report writing: six
weeks.
Qualifications: (i) Advanced degree in agriculture economics (minimum Master level) with a
specialization in farm management, and (ii) at least ten years experience in the design,
implementation and analysis of farm management surveys. (iii) An understanding of the problems
faced by economies in transition, preferably in eastern and central Europe.

REPUBLIC OF CROATIA
FARMERS SUPPORT SERVICES PROJECT
ANNEX C
PROJECT PROCUREMENT ARRANGEMENTS
1.        Project procurement arrangements are summarized in the Table C. 1 below and will be
undertaken in the following manner:
(i) Procurement of goods. The purchase of vehicles; computers; seed, grassland, and
veterinary laboratory equipment (excluding applied research related equipment; see
below, Procurement of Research Services); specialized farming equipment (for seed and
pasture variety trials); and milk and meat quality testing equipment would be carried
out through International Competitive Bidding (ICB) procedures in accordance with the
Bank's "Guidelines for Procurement Under IBRD Loans and IDA Credits" (January
1995). Contracts for goods estimated to cost US$300,000 or above would be procured
through ICB. Goods procured through ICB would constitute about 90 percent of cost
of Loan-financed goods. In the evaluation and comparison of bids for equipment to be
procured through ICB, Croatian manufactures would receive a domestic preference in
bid evaluation of 15 percent of the CIF price or the prevailing customs duty, whichever
is less, provided that a bidder offering goods manufactured in Croatia establishes to the
satisfaction of the Borrower and the Bank that (i) labor, raw materials and components
from within Croatia will account for more than 30 percent of the Ex-Works price of
the product offered; and (ii) the production facility in which those goods will be
manufactured or assembled has been engaged in manufacturing / assembling such goods
at least since the time of bid submission.
(ii)   The remaining 10 percent of Loan funded goods would be in minor packages suitable
for procurement methods other than ICB as follows:
(a)  National Competitive Bidding (NCB) for office furniture: two contracts
(financing amounting to approximately US$470,000) would be concluded using
Bank's NCB bidding documents for goods; there are numerous national
manufactures and traders of office furniture in Croatia ensuring competition in
the provision of these goods; also the size and the nature of the contracts is not
likely to generate foreign interest in bidding;
(b)  contracts for goods estimated to cost less than US$50,000 per contract (financing
amounting to US$280,000 in the aggregate), including audio-visual equipment,
small-scale irrigation equipment, herd performance recording equipment, and off-
the-shelf items such as office and training supplies, may be purchased through
National Shopping (NS), obtaining price quotations from at least three qualified
local suppliers; and

(c) National shopping: (aggregate amountfinanced $0.28 million) audio-visual equipment, small-scale irrigation equipment, and
herd recording equipment.
(d) National shopping: (aggregate amountfinanced US$0.049 million) for a single civil works contractfor estabUshment of smaU
genebank.
(e) Consultant services (aggregate amountfinanced US$ 1.68 milion) for advisors, national and international experts (in part
to prepare local training courses and curricula), and policy studies to be engaged in accordance with World Bank Guidelines
for the Use of Consultants. Consulting services to be grouped into six major contracts.
National advisors to be hired individually by farmer associations (aggregate amountfinanced US$0.76 million); total of 45
advisory contracts to be concluded.
() Training, at home and abroad, andfellowships (aggregate amountfinanced US$1.9 million). Local in-service training for
extension service staff, research staff, veterinary institute staff, carried out by MAF, ARC, NVI, NSA partiaUy in conjunction
with above consulting services; includes development of farmer based herd recording through CLSC.
Direct purchasing (aggregate amount financed US$0.340 milUon) of specialized research and extension publications and
journals (ranging from US$20 - 250).
National shopping (aggregate amount financed US$0.37 millon) for the publication of a farm management handbook; a
veterinary journal; and extension mass media packages (some 30 contracts up to US$30,000).
(g) Competitive Grant Research: (aggregate amountfinanced US$4.2 milion) for appUed agriculture research contracts awarded
to national qualfied research organizations based on research TORs established by ARC, research proposals submitted by
research organizations, evaluations carried out by independent research review panel (some 50 research contracts ranging
from US$50,000 to 150,000).



Project Implementation Plan                      - 129 -                                        ANNEX C
(iii) Procurement of works. Two civil works contracts would be carried out, consisting (i) of the
rehabilitation of the Sljeme Pasture Research Station, and the construction of the Pasture
Laboratory and Training Facility at said station; and (ii) the installation of a small seed bank at
the Faculty of Agronomy, University of Zagreb. The first contract (i.e., construction and
rehabilitation of Sljeme Pasture Research Station, estimated to cost US$904,000 (financing
US$796,000), would be procured following National Competitive Bidding (NCB) procedures in
accordance with Bank Procurement Guidelines. The issue of prequalifications would be discussed
at negotiations. The second civil works contract (i.e., installation of a gene bank), estimated to
cost US$56,000 (financing US$49,000), would be done following National Shopping procedures
for small works based on price quotations from at least three local qualified contractors. The local
construction industry is qualified to carry out such relatively simple civil works; also, it has been
established that sufficient competition exists amongst the local suppliers of civil works. Given the
remote location of the Sljeme Pasture Research Station, and the small value of the second
contract, it would not be likely to attract foreign bidders. A Country Procurement Assessment
Review (CPAR) for Croatia will be done following the passage by Parliament of its Public
Procurement Law. The CPAR is tentatively scheduled for early 1996. Meanwhile, the Bank's
NCB bidding documents for works will be used for the above -mentioned NCB contract.
(iv) Procurement of consulting services. Consultants for specialized and professional services financed
under the project would be selected in accordance with the Guidelines for the Use of Consultants
by World Bank Borrowers and by the Bank as Executing Agency (August 1981). These services
will be procured on the basis of shortlisting of qualified well-known firms, both international and
local. With the exception of a long term agriculture policy specialists, all individual consultancy
assignments are of a short term nature (between one to three months) and many include the
development of training programs and curricula.
2.        Specialized services would include six consulting contracts (estimated total cost US$1.84
million) for each of the project components. Each contract to be executed by international and national
consultants would include the following specialized services:
(i) extension: extension specialists, and skills training specialist;
(ii) research: applied research management specialist, applied research training specialist,
specialized agriculture research advisors;
(iii) animal health: veterinary epidemiologist, epidemiology data base specialist, whole herd
health advisor, computer programmer;
(iv)  grassland development: pasture resource inventory specialist, pasture/livestock economist,
grassland management specialist, pasture-based ruminant nutrition specialist;
(v)  seed industry development: seed certification specialist, seed industry regulations
specialist, seed testing and trials specialists; and
(vi)  policy analysis support: agriculture policy specialist, trade analyst, subsector policy
specialists and policy studies; and farm monitoring and market information activities.
3.        Included under item  (vi) para. 2 above (policy analysis support) but under separate
procurement arrangements are farm monitoring activities (aggregate finance US$100,000) and the
implementation of a market information system (aggregate finance US$100,000). Farm monitoring
activities including a baseline survey, and an annual farm survey would be commissioned directly from
the Institute of Agriculture Economic, Faculty of Agriculture, University of Zagreb. The Institute of
Agriculture Economics is currently the only entity in Croatia to have the experience, staff and capacity
to carry out detailed empirical work in rural areas. MAF would implement the Market Information



ANNEX C                                        - 130 -                       Project Implementation Plan
System through its Agriculture Policy Analysis Unit. The required TA, overseas training and computing
equipment for the establishment of the Market Information System would be procured through shortlisting
from a single qualified consulting firm.
4.        National advisors would be hired by private farmer associations under the Farmer Association
Advisor Pilot Scheme. Sufficient private sector advisors with the required qualifications are available in
Croatia because of their redundancy caused by the dismantling of the ex-social sector agro-kombinats and
will provide adequate competition. The advisors would be procured through advertising in the local press.
The advertisements announcing the need of the advisors will include their terns of reference, based on
standard terms of reference which will be reviewed by the Bank. MAF would prepare these standard
terms of reference and will submit them to the Bank for its review, prior to the publications of
advertisements. The appointment of the candidate selected by the farmer association would be subject to
MAF's approval.
5.        Procurement of training services and materials. To the extent feasible external fellowships
and training programs shall be included as part of the technical assistance packages procured from
consulting firms and training institutions; otherwise external fellowships and training would be awarded
on a direct contract basis with foreign institutions selected by MAF with the prior approval of the Bank.
In service, local training would be carried out by MAF, ARC, NVI, and NSA directly, or in
collaboration with national institutions on the basis of shortlisting with the assistance of the consultant
experts mentioned above. Prior to the beginning of it's fiscal year, during the life of the project, MAF
would prepare and submit to the Bank a detailed training and fellowship program for its review and
approval.
6.        Training materials which the Bank agrees are of a proprietary nature (e.g. technical
publications and journals/reference materials, computer software, etc.), may be acquired through Direct
Contracting from proprietors and/or copyright holders, in accordance with procedures acceptable to the
Bank. The aggregate financing of training materials procured through Direct Contracting amounts to
approximately US$340,000. Development and publication of a farm management handbook, a veterinary
journal, and approximately 30 extension mass media packages (aggregate amount financed approximately
US$370,000) would be done on the basis of National Shopping.
7.        Procurement of research services. The ARC would award research contracts (estimated to
range from US$50,000 to US$150,000) under a competitive grant arrangement financed from the
Agriculture Research Fund supported by the Bank's Loan. The ARC would make public invitations for
research proposals, specifying the type of research, the methodology, and the scope of research work to
be carried out. Qualified national research organizations and enterprises (both public and private sector)
are eligible to submit research proposals which will be judged with the support of independent reviewers,
consisting of a team of experts from MOST under the responsibility of ARC, on their technical merit and
price competitiveness, and the contract will be awarded by the ARC. MOST would be responsible for
supervising the contracted research services. Laboratory and analytical equipment would be included into
the research proposal and would become a factor of evaluation of proposals. For the implementation of
this component a detailed operational manual would be prepared by MAF with the technical assistance
financed under a Japanese Grant Fund; MAF would submit this manual to the Bank for review to meet
the condition of disbursement under this component.
8.       Incremental operating costs. Incremental operating costs would be fully financed by
Government with recurrent cost items procured in accordance with regular Government procedures.



Project Implementation Plan                   - 131 -                                      ANNEX C
9.        Procurement Review. The Bank would conduct a prior review of all ICB package and all the
first NCB and NS procurement packages for civil works, and the first NCB for goods. Prior Bank
approval would also be sought for all direct contracting. In addition, prior review would be undertaken
for all consulting contracts above US$100,000 (firms) and US$50,000 (individuals). The Bank's standard
bidding documents would be used for ICB packages and for the recruitment of consultants.
10.      Procurement information to be provided by the Borrower. The Borrower would promptly
inform the Bank of contract award and procurement issues and would include the following procurement
information in its progress reports:
(a) for equipment/materials, work contracts, technical assistance, training and study tours:
status and timing of all pending activities; and
(b) status of aggregate limits on specified methods of procurement.

ANNEX D                                      - 140 -                      Project Implementation Plan



REPUBLIC OF CROATIA
FARMERS SUPPORT SERVICES PROJECT
ANNEX E
SUMMARY FARM MODEL AND PROJECT ECONOMIC ANALYSIS
I. INTRODUCTION
1.    During project preparation in June 1994 nine farm models were constructed so as to:
*  illustrate and check the likely farm level technical and production impacts of project
activities such as improved extension, research,veterinary services and input(seed) supply.
*  assess the financial viability of the new technical options in a range of farming systems and
locations.
v  assess the economic implications of the expected changes.
At appraisal in March 1995, five of these models were selected and updated. This annex describes and
presents the results of the analysis of these five models. The remaining four models are available on
diskette; they are not considered here so as to avoid undue complexity. Staff of the Institute of
Agricultural Economics, Faculty of Agronomy, University of Zagreb, participated actively in the
specification and analysis of the models. The University has a regular farm survey program and
completed additional interviews to check data used in the models with farmers and processors. In
particular, Mr. J. Kraljickovic and Mr. J. Juracak contributed much of the data needed to build the
models.
2.    The models are indicative and it is believed that they reflect changes which are likely to occur
on farms which are exposed to more focused extension services and have access to improved management
advice, seed, livestock and other inputs. Details of the models summarized here are given in Annex N
of the supplemental volume.
II. MODEL DESCRIPTIONS
A. GENERAL
3.    The project aims to strengthen support services to farmers which will enable them to improve
production efficiency, management and marketing. The project will help farmers to focus on the farm
as a business and to respond to market changes by varying activity patterns and input levels, as well as
improving technical efficiency. The key to this approach is an effective extension service with a
commercial orientation and access to quality research and technical services.



ANNEX E                                         - 142 -                        Project Implementation Plan
4.    The crop and livestock budgets which form the basis of each farm or household model were
prepared in consultation with local agronomists and economists and checked by field discussion with
farmers, where possible. Generally they postulate crop yield increases of about 15 per cent with project
and include higher fertilizer, better seed inputs and improved livestock rations. Farm size has been held
constant between without and with project situations, although there are changes in cropping patterns
with project. The impact of investment to expand farm size, buy additional machinery or livestock or
to install irrigation, is examined separately in the proposed Rural Finance Pilot Project. Model farm size
is typically in the range 5 to 7 ha (except for intensive Dalmatia Vegetable model). This is a little larger
than average private farm size in these regions but there are many such farms and it is considered that
they are likely to respond first to improved support services.
5.    Most of the options available within FARMOD to model household level estimates were used
to provide a comprehensive description and assessment. Labor budgets show substantial annual surpluses
of family labor in all models, without and with project. Seasonal peaks in labor demand require use of
hired labor in the intensive vegetable models and most models do require incremental family labor with
project. Household consumption of farm produce has been included in each model and meets staple
grain, milk, egg and meat needs in most cases (exception high value vegetable model). Farm families will
have to draw upon the cash surpluses shown in each model to cover other food and living expenses.
Overhead costs are also included in each model to cover business expenses not readily allocated to
individual crop or livestock enterprises. Such costs are mostly in the range US$1,450 to US$1,800 per
farm and cover electricity, other fuel, land tax and insurance, tractor and equipment services and labor,
not related to individual crop activities.
6.    Very few private farms in Croatia have access to short or long term credit and so the financing
of production inputs in these models follows reality as both without and with project situations 100 per
cent of operating costs are financed by retained farm earnings from the previous year. Incremental
production costs typically lie in the range US$715 to US$2,200 per farm, or a little under half of the
expected gross value of incremental revenue. This is within the capacity of most model farms to finance,
either from without project retained earnings, from off-farm income or by moving to the with project
situation in steps over two or three years.
7.    Each model attempts to meet it's livestock feed needs from on-farm forage and crop production,
in line with usual practice in Croatia. There are exceptions for the vegetable model and some feed
additives and concentrates. Each model represents an individual farm and the with project situation has
not been phased in. The nature of most of the new technology proposed is such (better seeds, additional
fertilizer) that it is likely to be accepted promptly when the benefits are demonstrated clearly.
8.    The following five models are described in more detail below:
* Istria Mixed Farm Model
* Dalmatia Vegetable Farm Model
* Lika Mixed Farm Model
* Slavonija Crop Farm Model
* West Continental Dairy/Beef Farm Model



Project Implementation Plan                    - 143 -                                      ANNEX E
B. SPEcIc
Istria Mixed Farm Model
9.    This model may be applied to farms in the central area of the Istrian peninsular. Farms in this
area have opportunities to supply the local tourist industry and closer commercial ties to neighboring
countries than some other parts of Croatia. The model has a cropped area of 7.1 ha in both project
situations. The with project cropping pattern expands higher return potato and lucerne production and
deletes wheat and maize production so as to avoid large increments in labor or land use. Improved
technology is applied to barley, potato and lucerne production in the with project situation. Istria
traditionally provides hay and forage seeds to adjacent mountain areas and has adequate markets for
increased potato production. Although livestock activities comprise almost half of the gross value of
production no incremental livestock income is assumed, as it focuses on higher value crops.
10.   Family labor requirements increase from 1,220 hours per year to 1,410 hours with project, an
increment of 190 hours. This still leaves a large surplus which can be used in part to gain employment
in the tourist industry.
Dalmatia Vegetable Farm Model
11.   Dalmatia has a successful and expanding vegetable industry in part due to a warmer climate which
enables early harvest and access to high price, out-of-season markets in other parts of Croatia and nearby
countries. One of the main limits to expansion of production is a shortage of irrigation water and
investment to make better use of water is examined separately in the proposed Rural Finance Project. No
such investment is considered in this project. Joint marketing of vegetables is also being explored by
farmers in Dalmatia.
12.   This model has a small farm area of 1.2 ha but has by far the highest net value of production
of any model due to the focus on early tomato and potato crops and other vegetables. There are no
changes of cropping pattern assumed for the with project situation but crop yields are increased by 10
per cent mainly in response to higher fertilizer and manure inputs. Livestock are produced for home
consumption and there are no increments with project.
13.   Incremental family labor with project (to handle larger harvests) is 191 hour per year. Although
there is substantial unused family labor, hired labor is needed to meet seasonal peaks of demand and this
also increases with project, by 33 hours per year.
Lika Mixed Farm Model
14.   Lika is a mountainous area with much pasture land and some emphasis on livestock production.
The proposed Rural Finance Pilot Project includes a specialist sheep production model but this model
looks at changes in a mixed farm with crop, cattle and pig production. The model increases potato and
reduces wheat production with project in response to crop budget financial profitability; additionally dairy
cow numbers are increased from 3 to 4 and cheese making (600 kg per year) is introduced with project.
Financing is discussed in 3.2.3 below. There is a strong demand for local cheeses and the necessary skills
and interest in increasing production are available. Potato and barley yields are increased by about 15
per cent with project in response to use of better seed and more fertilizer.



ANNEX E                                        - 144 -                       Project Implementation Plan
15.   The cropped area is constant at 5.8 ha in both project situations and is below total farm area
of 7.9 ha to allow for rotation and non-arable land.
16.   This model has the greatest increment in family labor input with project, 631 hour per year.
However with project labor is still only about half estimated available labor and most of the increment
is in high value cheese production yielding incremental hourly returns more than double average without
project returns.
Slavonija Crop Farm Model
17.   Slavonija is the major crop production region in Croatia. This model is representative of private
farms which are replacing the Agro-Kombinats as major producers in the region. The cropping pattern
changes with project to reduce sugar beet and maize area and to expand soybean, so as to improve self-
sufficiency in pig feed. Wheat, meadow and barley are constant, as is the total cropped area of 5.3 ha.
Almost half of the crops produced (by value) are used on-farm for livestock production. The model
includes 1 cow, 6 sows and a small poultry activity (no increment with project). Of these, the pig activity
is the main commercial livestock activity; with project weaner pig production increases by about 13 per
cent and ration costs are reduced. Crop yield increases of just under 15 per cent are achieved with better
fertilizer inputs and seeds.
18.   Family labor use in this model is near constant with and without project. The yield increases do
not demand additional labor as harvest is mechanized and the changes in cropping pattern do not create
new labor demands.
West Continental Dairy/Beef Farm Model
19.   This model has four Simmental cows in both project situations. Milk production increases from
2,800 1 to 3,360 1 per cow per year with project. Improved animal health, changed rations and better
genetic material are expected to be accessible through improved extension and veterinary services. The
cropped area remains constant at 4.3 ha but the pattern changes with project. Maize silage and mixed
grass pasture are introduced to boost feed supply with project and maize for grain and the less productive
meadow are reduced slightly. Mixed grass and other improved pastures would be stimulated by project
activities and gradually displace meadow and other unimproved pastures. Further increases in technical
and financial performance are possible, e.g. use of milk replacer for calf rearing or breed changes, and
practical but have not been considered as they are still uncommon in Croatia.
20.   Family labor requirements are virtually the same with and without project and are around 40 per
cent of estimated available labor. There is scope to expand the size of farms of this type but this is not
considered within this project. Increased farm size plus use of milk replacer would have a big positive
impact on milk collection costs and overall dairy industry efficiency.
III. FARM MODEL FINANCIAL ANALYSIS
A. GENERAL
21.   The farm gate fmancial prices used in this analysis are those which prevailed in the main
production region for each item during March 1995. Minor seasonal adjustments were made and some
averaging was employed where prices differed between main producing regions. All analysis has been



Project Implementation Plan                                       - 145 -                                                         ANNEX  E
completed in constant 1995 DEM; the apparent precision in some prices results from conversion of a
Kuna price quote to DEM at the March 1995 exchange rate. The prices used provide reliable farm gate
values for the expected incremental production. However it is clear that new marketing systems are being
developed and that prices do fluctuate from place to place and time to time.
22.      Each model shows net incremental farm  rmancial benefits which are likely to be attractive to
farmers in relation to the required additional purchased inputs and family labor. The analysis was for a
10 year period and the discount rate was set at 10 per cent. Labor returns in US$ per hour are
maintained or increased with project in each model. There are no additional investments required in the
models beyond the short term funding of crop and livestock inputs. When future financial cash flows are
discounted at 10 per cent, strong NPV's result. Switching values before financing at 10 per cent indicate
that in all models revenues can fall by at least 50 per cent or operating costs increase by at least 100
percent, before NPV falls to zero.
